Let me compile everything.\n\n---\n\n## Comprehensive Secrets & Credential Management Report\n\n### Overview\n\nCredentials are managed across four projects: **jira** (Claude agent orchestration system), **infra** (BlindHash/Hetzner infrastructure), **enterprise-ng** (Anchore Enterprise NG service code), and **autonomy** (AGI platform vision). Each project has a distinct approach, ranging from mature file-based encryption in infra to ad-hoc dotfile injection in jira.\n\n---\n\n## 1. Claude Auth Tokens — jira project\n\n**What they are:** The Claude CLI's session credentials: `~/.claude.json` (config) and `~/.claude/.credentials.json` (OAuth tokens that Claude Code uses to authenticate with Anthropic's API).\n\n**How they are stored:** On the host filesystem at `$HOME/.claude/` — outside the repo, protected by `.gitignore`. Never baked into Docker images.\n\n**How they are injected into containers:** Via `start_agent.sh` at container startup time (lines 52–70 of that script):\n\n```bash\nCLAUDE_CREDS_DIR=\"${CLAUDE_CREDENTIALS_DIR:-$HOME/.claude}\"\nCLAUDE_CFG_FILE=\"${CLAUDE_CONFIG_FILE:-$HOME/.claude.json}\"\n\ndocker exec \"agent-${AGENT_ID}\" mkdir -p /root/.claude\ndocker cp \"$CLAUDE_CFG_FILE\" \"agent-${AGENT_ID}:/root/.claude.json\"\ndocker cp \"${CLAUDE_CREDS_DIR}/.credentials.json\" \\\n    \"agent-${AGENT_ID}:/root/.claude/.credentials.json\"\n```\n\nThe paths are configured via two environment variables in `/home/jeremy/jira/.env`:\n```bash\nCLAUDE_CREDENTIALS_DIR=$HOME/.claude\nCLAUDE_CONFIG_FILE=$HOME/.claude.json\n```\n\n**Security properties:** Injected at runtime, not baked into images. The `.env` file itself is bind-mounted read-only into containers (`/home/jeremy/jira/.env:/jira/.env:ro`). The credentials are copied into ephemeral containers that are destroyed after each agent run.\n\n---\n\n## 2. Anthropic API Key — jira project (Slack bot)\n\n**What it is:** `sk-ant-...` — direct Anthropic API key used by the Slack bot's Python code to call Claude Haiku for intent classification.\n\n**How it's stored:** In `/home/jeremy/jira/.env.slack` (a separate env file, not the main `.env`):\n```bash\nSLACK_BOT_TOKEN=xoxb-...\nSLACK_APP_TOKEN=xapp-...\nANTHROPIC_API_KEY=sk-ant-...\nAGENT_POOL_SIZE=2\nJIRA_DIR=/home/jeremy/jira\n```\n\n**How it's consumed:** Via `os.getenv(\"ANTHROPIC_API_KEY\")` in `tools/slack/config.py`. The Slack bot runs on the host (not in a container), so it reads these env vars directly from the dotenv file.\n\n**Note:** The ANTHROPIC_API_KEY is distinct from Claude Code's credentials — the former is a raw API key for the `anthropic` Python SDK; the latter is an OAuth session token managed by the Claude CLI.\n\n---\n\n## 3. JIRA API Token — jira project\n\n**What it is:** An Atlassian API token for reading JIRA tickets (fetching ticket content, posting comments).\n\n**How it's stored:** `~/.jira_token` file with `chmod 600`. Optionally configured as `JIRA_TOKEN_FILE=$HOME/.jira_token` in the main `.env` file.\n\n**How containers access it:** The `.env` file is bind-mounted into agent containers, and shell tools reading `JIRA_TOKEN_FILE` resolve the path. The `run_agent.sh` orchestrator sources the `.env` before passing parameters:\n```bash\nsource /home/jeremy/jira/.env\n# AGENT_WORKSPACE=\"/home/jeremy/agents\"\n# JIRA_BASE_URL, JIRA_TOKEN, etc.\n```\n\n---\n\n## 4. GitHub Tokens / SSH Keys — jira project\n\n**How git access works:** The agent repositories are pre-cloned on the host under `AGENT_WORKSPACE` (e.g., `/home/jeremy/agents/`), then bind-mounted into containers. Containers get read-only access to the workspace. No runtime git cloning requires tokens inside containers.\n\n**SSH access for private repos:** AnchoreCTL's development guide requires `Git SSH Access` for private `github.com/anchore/enterprise` modules, handled via `make bootstrap-git`. This runs on the host, not in containers.\n\n**Summary:** git credentials are handled by host-level SSH agent forwarding and pre-cloned workspaces — not by injecting tokens into containers.\n\n---\n\n## 5. Slack Bot Tokens — jira project\n\n**What they are:** Two tokens from Slack's Socket Mode integration:\n- `SLACK_BOT_TOKEN` (`xoxb-...`) — bot OAuth token for posting messages, calling Slack API\n- `SLACK_APP_TOKEN` (`xapp-...`) — app-level token for Socket Mode WebSocket connection\n\n**How they're stored:** In `/home/jeremy/jira/.env.slack`:\n```bash\nSLACK_BOT_TOKEN=xoxb-...\nSLACK_APP_TOKEN=xapp-...\n```\n\n**How they're consumed:** `os.getenv()` in `tools/slack/config.py`. The Slack bot runs as a persistent host process (`python -m tools.slack`), reading from the dotenv file at startup via `python-dotenv`.\n\n**Creation process:** Tokens are obtained from `api.slack.com/apps` — create app from manifest, enable Socket Mode, install to workspace, copy both tokens.\n\n---\n\n## 6. Environment Variables Injected into Agent Containers — jira project\n\nA complete inventory of what gets into agent containers at startup:\n\n| Variable | Source | Mechanism |\n|---|---|---|\n| `CLAUDE_CREDENTIALS_DIR` / `CLAUDE_CONFIG_FILE` | Host `~/.env` | `docker cp` at startup |\n| Claude credentials files | Host `~/.claude/` | `docker cp` into `/root/.claude/` |\n| JIRA env vars (URL, email, token path) | `/home/jeremy/jira/.env` | Bind-mounted at `/jira/.env:ro` |\n| Anchore API credentials | Set by test env | Exported env vars before test runs |\n| `ANCHORECTL_URL/USERNAME/PASSWORD` | Host env / test scripts | Exported before running E2E tests |\n| `DOCKER_USER/DOCKER_PASS` | Host env / test scripts | Exported for registry operations |\n| `REGRESSION_TEST_DEFAULT_API_*` | Host env / test scripts | Exported for regression tests |\n| `WORKLOAD` | `run_agent.sh` argument | Passed as container env var |\n\nThe `/home/jeremy/jira/.env` bind-mount is the primary mechanism. Credentials in it propagate into every tool script that sources it inside the container.\n\n---\n\n## 7. Failed / Painful Credential Management — jira project\n\nNo explicit \"credential management failed\" incidents were found in the graph. However, several structural pain points are visible:\n\n- **The `docker cp` credential injection is brittle**: If `~/.claude/.credentials.json` doesn't exist or has expired OAuth tokens, the agent silently gets no auth. There's no validation step.\n- **Two separate env files**: `/.env` and `.env.slack` must both be configured correctly. Easy to miss one.\n- **JIRA token as a flat file**: `~/.jira_token` with `chmod 600` is fine for one machine but doesn't scale across agents or machines.\n- **Agent pool pre-warming**: The `warmup_agent.sh` pre-starts containers, but credentials must still be injected each time. If Claude tokens expire between warmup and use, the agent fails mid-execution (5-10 min in).\n- **No rotation mechanism**: No documented process for rotating any of these credentials. If JIRA token or Slack tokens expire, manual update of flat files is required.\n\n---\n\n## 8. enterprise-ng Project — Database Credentials and Service Auth\n\n**Database credentials:** The Anchore Enterprise NG services use a `DbConfig` Pydantic model:\n\n```python\nclass DbConfig(BaseModel):\n    host: str              # PostgreSQL host\n    port: int = 5432       # PostgreSQL port\n    user: str              # Database user\n    password: str          # Database password\n    database: str          # Database name\n    db_connect_args: Dict[str, Any] = {}\n```\n\n**How configured:** Via YAML configuration at `/config/config.yaml` with environment variable substitution. The `loader.py` module processes `${VARIABLE_NAME}` patterns:\n- `ANCHORE_*`-prefixed vars: optional — missing ones are silently dropped from config\n- Non-`ANCHORE_*` vars: required — missing ones raise `EnvVarNotFoundError`\n\n**Development credentials:** Hardcoded `admin`/`foobar` throughout E2E test infrastructure and `postgres`/`mysecretpassword` in test commands. These are expected dev-only values, not production secrets.\n\n**Known bug (flagged in code review):** In `enterprise/services/component_catalog/service.py:149-152`, the PostgreSQL connection URL is built with:\n```python\nf\"postgresql://{db_config.user}:{db_config.password}@...\"\n```\nThis will break if the password contains special characters (e.g., `@`, `#`, `/`) that need URL encoding. Flagged as a non-blocking warning in PR reviews.\n\n**Service-to-service auth (anchorectl/API layer):** The `anchorectl` CLI and Anchore Enterprise API use HTTP Basic Auth. The Go client injects credentials via:\n```go\nctx := client.Enterprise.AuthorizedContext(context.Background())\n```\nThis reads username/password from AnchoreCTL's config (typically `~/.anchorectl/config.yaml` or env vars `ANCHORECTL_USERNAME`/`ANCHORECTL_PASSWORD`).\n\n**Worker config passdown:** Workers receive a `WorkerStartupData` struct containing the full `RootConfig`. Config — including database credentials — is serialized to JSON and passed to subprocess workers at startup. No separate secrets channel; everything goes through `RootConfig`.\n\n---\n\n## 9. infra Project — BlindHash Hetzner Infrastructure\n\nThis is the most mature secrets management approach across all projects.\n\n**Core mechanism — asymmetric encryption with a master password:**\n\nAll secrets are encrypted asymmetrically using an RSA public key and decrypted with `openssl smime`:\n```bash\nexport HCLOUD_TOKEN=$(openssl smime -decrypt -binary -inform DER \\\n    -inkey ~/infra/pki/encrypt/private-key-encrypted.pem \\\n    < ~/infra/secrets/hcloud-token.enc)\n```\n\nThe private key (`pki/encrypt/private-key-encrypted.pem`) is itself protected by a passphrase with 50 million PBKDF2 iterations (deliberately slow, ~10 seconds to decrypt). Scripts always start with:\n```\n[...] Decrypting private key (this may take a moment — 50M PBKDF2 iterations)...\nEnter pass phrase for /home/jeremy/infra/pki/encrypt/private-key-encrypted.pem:\n[...] Private key decrypted\n[...] hcloud authenticated\n[...] Decrypting secrets...\n[...] All secrets decrypted\n```\n\n**Complete secrets inventory (encrypted `.enc` files in `secrets/`):**\n\n| Secret | File | Used By |\n|---|---|---|\n| Hetzner Cloud API token | `secrets/hcloud-token.enc` | `lib/common.sh` → all ops scripts |\n| Tailscale OAuth client_id + client_secret | `secrets/tailscale-oauth.enc` | `lib/common.sh` → Tailscale registration |\n| LUKS pool volume passphrase | `secrets/luks-pool.enc` | `recover-worker.sh` → decrypt data volumes |\n| B2 (Backblaze) backup key | (implied from bootstrap session) | `bootstrap-frontend-volumes.sh` |\n\n**SSH key infrastructure (4 identities on workstation):**\n\n| Key | Accesses | Rationale |\n|---|---|---|\n| `id_ed25519` | All front-ends (CA-signed cert), snapshot build servers | Primary key; CA cert gives fleet-wide access |\n| `blindhash-worker` | All workers via ProxyJump | Isolated from CA PKI — workers don't trust the CA |\n| `claude_docker` | ubuntu-1/2/4, ubuntu-5/6/7/8, xs23-1 | Legacy servers, pre-CA era |\n| (4th) | (additional identity) | Context incomplete |\n\n**GitHub access:** Previously used `gh CLI auth` in `bootstrap-frontend-volumes.sh`. Was replaced with `git credential.helper store` + a `.git-credentials` file as a more robust mechanism for cloning 8 bare repos from GitHub onto the frontend code volume.\n\n**Auth material audit finding (critical gap identified in session c4f68058):**\n\n> \"If you pull the infra repo on a brand new workstation and know the decryption password, can you fully rebuild everything? **Answer: No. You're dead in the water. You can't SSH into a single server.**\"\n\nWhat IS recoverable from repo + password: encryption public key, hcloud token (via `hcloud-token.enc`), Tailscale OAuth credentials, LUKS passphrase.\n\nWhat is NOT in the repo: the SSH private keys themselves (they live only on `~/.ssh/` on the workstation). CA-signed certificates are perishable and must be reissued. This is the fundamental bootstrap problem — the SSH keys needed to access servers to install new SSH keys are not stored anywhere except the workstation.\n\n**LUKS encryption for data volumes:** Pool volumes on Hetzner workers are LUKS-encrypted at rest. The passphrase is stored in `secrets/luks-pool.enc`, decrypted locally on the workstation, delivered to each worker over SSH into a tmpfs mount during `recover-worker.sh`, then shredded. Volumes are locked on reboot — explicit workstation involvement required to unlock.\n\n**TLS certificate management:** `scripts/lego/renew-certs.sh` handles automated TLS cert renewal, installed as a cron job on frontend servers.\n\n**Ops TUI:** A Python/Textual workstation-only console (`scripts/tui/`) authenticates using the same password→private key→hcloud flow. Acts as a GUI wrapper around the same secret decryption infrastructure.\n\n---\n\n## 10. Autonomy Network Vision — Secret Management\n\nThe autonomy project contains Oct-Nov 2024 vision docs. The knowledge graph has a summary:\n\n> \"README.md — Founding vision. An AGI platform called 'Alice' that runs as a network of nodes. Users contribute compute, get intelligence services. **Cryptographic identity, attestation**, model-agnostic fabric, priority queues per user.\"\n\nThe vision explicitly calls for cryptographic identity and attestation at the node level. No concrete implementation exists yet — the project is pure vision/design docs. There is no mention of specific vault, keyring, or encryption schemes in the design notes. The operative design principle is that agents get pre-authorized CLI tools in a secure mesh with minimal context — secrets should be pre-baked into the tool environment, not passed through agent prompts.\n\n---\n\n## 11. Summary: What Works, What's Broken, What's Needed\n\n### What works well\n\n- **infra's asymmetric encryption pattern** is the most robust: a single master password unlocks an RSA private key, which decrypts all other secrets. Resistant to repo compromise. Deliberate key-stretching (50M PBKDF2 iterations) slows brute-force.\n- **jira's credential isolation** (never baked into images, injected at startup, `.gitignore` protection) is the right architecture even if the mechanism is basic.\n- **enterprise-ng's env-var substitution in YAML** (`${ANCHORE_DB_HOST}`) is clean and standard for 12-factor app patterns.\n\n### What's broken or painful\n\n- **infra SSH bootstrap problem**: SSH private keys aren't recoverable from the repo. A new workstation requires manual key migration or server-side re-authorization. This is acknowledged in the audit but unresolved.\n- **jira credential fragility**: `docker cp` of Claude credentials has no validation. Expired tokens silently fail mid-agent-run (after 5-10 min). No automated token refresh or detection.\n- **Proliferating env files**: jira has at least two dotenv files (`.env` and `.env.slack`) plus a flat token file (`~/.jira_token`). No unified management.\n- **enterprise-ng DB password bug**: f-string URL construction without URL-encoding will silently break with special-character passwords.\n- **No rotation automation**: None of the three projects has automated credential rotation. JIRA tokens, Slack tokens, Anthropic API keys all require manual updates when expired.\n- **GitHub access fragility in infra**: The `gh auth`→`credential.helper store` migration shows iterative patching rather than a clean solution.\n\n### Requirements for a unified secret management system\n\nBased on all observed patterns, a unified system would need:\n\n1. **Single unlock ceremony**: One master password (or hardware key) unlocks everything, as in infra's current design — but extended to cover the SSH bootstrap gap.\n2. **Per-secret scoping**: Secrets have declared consumers (jira-agent, slack-bot, infra-hetzner). No credential grants access beyond its declared scope.\n3. **Injection without prompt exposure**: Secrets injected into tool environments (env vars, files in tmpfs) but never passed through LLM context/prompts. The current `docker cp` approach is correct in principle.\n4. **Token health validation**: Before container startup, verify Claude credentials are valid and not expired. Surface failures before the 10-minute agent run begins.\n5. **Rotation tracking**: Expiry dates for all tokens (JIRA API tokens expire, Slack tokens can be revoked, Anthropic keys can be rotated). Alert before expiry.\n6. **SSH key recovery path**: The infra bootstrap gap needs a solution — either store encrypted SSH private keys in the repo (encrypted with the same asymmetric key) or document a multi-step bootstrap sequence that doesn't assume workstation key survival.\n7. **Audit trail**: Which agent used which credential, when. Especially important for containers running Claude with write access to codebases.\n8. **LUKS-style encryption for agent workspaces**: The infra pattern of encrypting data at rest and delivering keys transiently (tmpfs + shred) is the right model for agent workspace isolation too."}],"stop_reason":"end_turn","stop_sequence":null,"usage":{"input_tokens":1,"cache_creation_input_tokens":2107,"cache_read_input_tokens":112612,"output_tokens":4514,"server_tool_use":{"web_search_requests":0,"web_fetch_requests":0},"service_tier":"standard","cache_creation":{"ephemeral_1h_input_tokens":0,"ephemeral_5m_input_tokens":2107},"inference_geo":"","iterations":[],"speed":"standard"}},"requestId":"req_011CZ5mgZQvPWY2xLeTjpSz5","type":"assistant","uuid":"a422c7c5-00ef-4713-9969-82e5eb04a33c","timestamp":"2026-03-15T23:58:36.950Z","userType":"external","cwd":"/home/jeremy/workspace/autonomy","sessionId":"2abe4914-4667-4652-81ab-55caca3b9ac8","version":"2.1.76","gitBranch":"HEAD","slug":"radiant-sauteeing-token"}
